- **References:** `<e224fa77.0401280245.1fd41f48@posting.google.com> <naKdnYuz8smKmoTdRVn-uQ@giganews.com> <qdbSb.12657$oN3.5870@newssvr24.news.prodigy.com> <Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com> <e224fa77.0401300657.69af4f36@posting.google.com> <BzASb.3777$F23.1956@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
If you're having performance problems using searches, consider alternatives.  
Virtual memory is pretty efficient.  How about real large tables or resident
files and some type of keyed or hash mechanism to find your match?
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Performance in perform loops

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "James" <magogrwr@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2004-02-11T19:17:22-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<SuzWb.37908$8a5.17171@bignews1.bellsouth.net>`
- **References:** `<e224fa77.0401280245.1fd41f48@posting.google.com> <naKdnYuz8smKmoTdRVn-uQ@giganews.com> <qdbSb.12657$oN3.5870@newssvr24.news.prodigy.com> <Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com> <e224fa77.0401300657.69af4f36@posting.google.com>`

```
Then MAYBE, just maybe, this module IS where the bulk of the work is done!
Especially if as you say
this contains complex rules.  That is the way a well designed program
usually runs.
some % in I/O
some % in exceptions
the majority in one or two portions
Sometimes we expect something just because and fail to question if our
expectation is valid!

If you check your JCL listing very carefully (provided it has that info
there and it should)
you can see how much time is spent in I/O, and waits, paging.

Also, why can't you order the Table, even if you can't do a SEARCH ALL, you
can
still check the previous compare-item against the current to see where you
should START
your SEARCH.

If you need to apply /check very many of these rules sequentially one after
the other, then
you do need to determine where to start each time.

P.S.
I doubt that the table isn't paged in/out unless you have more than 96
Megabytes of memory AND
the program runs all by itself.

Really large systems (the largest credit card processor in world has 96 MB
in one region and that includes PROD/TEST)
generally have 64 to 96 Megabytes of memory which this table has
1/6 to 1/4 - add in code, buffers, OS etc and you ARE getting paged!

BTW Jerry M. I calculated the table size at 11,600,000 bytes
as follows
05  TB-ABG-FELD-INDEX         PIC S9(9) COMP.   4 bytes
05  TB-ABG-FELDNR             PIC S9(9) COMP.       4 bytes
05  TB-ABG-OPERATOR           PIC X.                      1 byte
05  TB-ABG-ABGRVON            PIC X(10).                10 bytes
05  TB-ABG-ABGRBIS            PIC X(10).                    10 bytes
= 29 bytes
```

```
Bottom posting

m6v100@web.de (Joern) wrote in message news:<e224fa77.0401310333.17daf522@posting.google.com>...
> jacksleight@hotmail.com (Jack Sleight) wrote in message news:<8a2d426e.0401300702.63bc43b3@posting.google.com>...
> > "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> wrote in message news:<Iaednatqpp4xAYTdRVn-tA@giganews.com>...
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> Best regards Joern

Hell Joern

Again, I think the compile options look reasonable (I should have
asked this question myself!), though I haven't looked very deeply.

I do see that you have SQL(DB2) amongst your settings.  If this means
that you have DB2, or any other RDBMS database for that matter, then
this problem may be a very good application for two tables with
multiple indexes on the relevant fields ascending and descending as
appropriate.  You might even get the solution into a single statement!
 However, I couldnt be sure that it would take any less time and might
even take a lot more more time to execute.  Nevertheless, I think it
could be worth investigating with the aid of an SQL guru, to ensure
that the appropriate tables and queries are properly set up and taking
advantage of indexes, etc appropriately.

Kind regards,

Robert
```

```
In article <bfdfc3e8.0401312126.5ca862f1@posting.google.com>, Thane
Hubbell <thaneh@softwaresimple.com> wrote:

> 
> I know this wasn't directed to me, but....  This is a ODD thing, OO
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
The same was said about "Quantum Theory". So what!

> Until you have the "AHA" lightbulb goes on experiece, you just don't
> get it.  Sorry - that's the way it is.  When you DO get it -
> everything will fall into place and the SIMPLICITY and EASE of it will
> become plain.  At it's core it IS simple, and that is it's elegence.
>
I've had the AHA experience. I too think that the theory is elegent and
very simple in it's logic. However, it's premise, that of creating a
language tailored to the problem domain will make the programming of
that domain easier and more efficient is false.
> That said - where I think the FAILING is, is not in the concept of OO,
> but in it's implementation by programmers.  If it is not properly
> managed, one loses some of the advantages.  Properly managed, however,
> it becomes a powerful paradigm.
> 
There is nothing wrong with the paradigm, it just confers other
unforeseen problems in the place of the problems it solves.
It then becomes a value judgement as to which approach is "better".
This can be seen in the experiences of those who implement the theory.
Why is it that you think there is a failure to implement properly?
Perhaps it's not a EASY or elegant as it seems. As we all know, it's
extremely easy to get a bad implementation in any programming task. Why
is it so hard to get a GOOD implementation in OO? After all, the vast
majority of programmer are by definition not the programming equivalent
of "Einstein's". Why is it that the "proponents" of OO are pointing to
this unnatural, hard to get right programming method. You would have
thought that the next language to become de'rigur would have catered to
all those programmers that just program for a living and not for life!

It seems that the goal of the designers of COBOL has been tossed out.
Their goal was to design a language that the average clerk in a company
could use. In this it appears that they have achieved their goals
admirably. Why do modern language designers not design a language that
is obvious, easy, powerfull and can be used by anyone without the need
to tack half the letters of the alphabet behind their name?

> Is it really NEW or is it "libraries" and such repackaged?  No - it is
> really "NEW" - or as new as something over 30 years old can be.
> 
> I think OO is the only thing debated more than the death of COBOL.
I rest my case. If it were so obvious there would be no debate.

It's like the Physists search for the "theory of everything". They
think that when they get it right, it will be so obvious that everyone
will get it at once without the need for years of study.
```

```
Joseph Katnic <usrr@post.no.mail> wrote in message news:<010220042136098148%usrr@post.no.mail>...

> Why is it that you think there is a failure to implement properly?
> Perhaps it's not a EASY or elegant as it seems. As we all know, it's
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

The value of the paradigm comes from "knowing what you have" to build
on.  The failure comes from forgetting what bricks you have already
invented to build on.  Polymorphism fails when you don't know what you
have to begin with.  Most times OO systems collapse under their own
weight because of frequent re-invention of things already there.  It
gets too confusing.  This is not an OO failure - it's a failure in
implementation.  That's my point.

> It seems that the goal of the designers of COBOL has been tossed out.
> Their goal was to design a language that the average clerk in a company
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

I for one have not lost this perspective.  In fact, I tried and tried
to understand OO over and over again - but it wasn't until I
experienced OO as defined in the 2002 standard, that I had my AHA
experience.  OO COBOL is very very simple.
```

```
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> implementation.  That's my point.

But "frequent re-invention of things already there" may be OO's saving grace. 
Sometimes it is better to have many different bricks than one brick that can do
it all.   Sometimes it is too dangerous to morph an existing foundation of the
building so that it can do just one more task.

Realizing that just because re-use can be useful sometimes - it can be costly
other times - is vital.
```

```
an argument.  COBOL by it's nature tends to foster sound Data

does matter is that OO design is a DIFFERENT process.  One cannot use
the same old methods used procedurally to design using OO.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OO? Oh oh!

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Peter E.C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T02:07:48+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<401e4c56_4@news.athenanews.com>`
- **References:** `<SOyRb.121471$6y6.2401423@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <4016e8da_6@news.athenanews.com> <Q0_Rb.502$zv7.75942111@newssvr11.news.prodigy.com> <bfdfc3e8.0401312126.5ca862f1@posting.google.com> <010220042136098148%usrr@post.no.mail>`

```
A few gentle comments, Joe... <G>

"Joseph Katnic" <usrr@post.no.mail> wrote in message
news:010220042136098148%usrr@post.no.mail...
> In article <bfdfc3e8.0401312126.5ca862f1@posting.google.com>, Thane
> Hubbell <thaneh@softwaresimple.com> wrote:
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> The same was said about "Quantum Theory". So what!

It was said about Quantum Mechanics over 30 years ago... Much has happened
since, and today's understanding is different from the understanding (or
lack of it) then. Niels Bohr said: "Anyone who is not shocked by quantum
mechanics hasn't understood it". (He was right. As my understanding of this
subject has grown over many years, I have become more and more shocked. <G>.
I still find it shocking... but that doesn't mean it can't be understood.

That isn't what Thane's saying at all. He's saying (and I agree with him),
that when you DO understand OO, it is a Revelation.

So what?! So, I agree with Thane's assertion that you haven't understood OO,
if you think it is just old stuff repackaged.
>
> > Until you have the "AHA" lightbulb goes on experiece, you just don't
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> that domain easier and more efficient is false.

I don't believe that is the premise of OO. Could be the premise of some OO
based languages, but not OO itself.

> > That said - where I think the FAILING is, is not in the concept of OO,
> > but in it's implementation by programmers.  If it is not properly
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> Why is it that you think there is a failure to implement properly?

Because all too often there are other motivations at work. My experience has
been that when OO projects are managed properly, they ARE successful. If
people are not properly trained, if they are pressed to provide an exemplary
solution for a Business Critical project the first time they try, if the
Project standards and Management Methodology are still those used for the
usual COBOL development, there is a pretty fair chance of failure. The
pundits walk away with smug "I told you so" looks, and the failed project
team is too demoralised to do it again. Besides "Everybody Knows" that it
has failed so why invest any more time in it?
If you ensure that people have had time to grasp the principles of OO, if
you allow some experimentation in a blame free culture on a non-critical
project, if you support them, use RAD type iterative, interactive,
development instead of the bloody Waterfall, confidence grows in both
programmers and users. Users grasp OO much quicker than COBOL programmers,
on the whole. It's because they are used to using Business Objects every
day. They have no problem with classifying and categorizing groups of
objects, and are not blinded by preconceived ideas about calling subroutines
and passing parameters.

I'm not describing some Utopian dream; I've seen it and done it. It works.
And OO works too, when it is properly implemented (exactly as Thane
suggested.)

> Perhaps it's not a EASY or elegant as it seems. As we all know, it's
> extremely easy to get a bad implementation in any programming task. Why
> is it so hard to get a GOOD implementation in OO?

Ask the Java programmers of the World why they have never written a GOOD
implementation. It is no harder to do it in OO than in anything else ONCE
YOU UNDERSTAND OO. But, as I have remaked here many times before,
understanding OO takes effort and requires change. (At least, it does for
procedural programmers like COBOL and PL/1 people; people with NO prior
programming knowledge take to it like ducks to water, once you cut through
the jargon...)

>After all, the vast
> majority of programmer are by definition not the programming equivalent
> of "Einstein's".

Neither are they the programming equivalent of Homer Simpson. (Doh!) I find
that treating them as intelligent professionals (even when they occasionally
are not) gets much better results than the alternative.

Fortunately, the average OO programmer is neither a Simpson nor an Einstein,
and doesn't need to be. (Much like the average COBOL programmer, really. It
is simply a different skill set.)


> Why is it that the "proponents" of OO are pointing to
> this unnatural, hard to get right programming method.

Because it ISN'T unatural, or "hard to get right" if you invest some effort
and keep an open mind when acquiring it. Even just setting aside the belief
that what you already know is the only possible way to program computers,
can have startling results.

> You would have
> thought that the next language to become de'rigur would have catered to
> all those programmers that just program for a living and not for life!

Languages are made "de rigeur" by Management, who, in turn, for the  most
part, are heavily influenced by what they read in the computer press, or
hear from their peers at Mickey Mouse Megabucks Corporation, or even what
their opposition are doing in IT. It's a bit like the old IBM syndrome that
was rampant in the 60s and 70s... IT Manager commissions independent advice
and decides to buy IBM. Shop Floor knows the software is crap, hardware,
while very reliable, is not exactly cutting edge,  and there are much better
products (hardware and software) on the market. But the Manager knows
"nobody ever got fired for buying IBM...". If the whole thing goes pants, he
can go to the Board and say: "Hey, I bought the best in the World... What
more could I do?"

As Board members read newspapers and they all know about IBM, his job is
safe.

Meantime the Shop Floor get on with it. It's a living...

Don't blame technology and the rightnmess or wrongness of it for what is "de
rigeur"; these are political decisions that have nothing whatever to do with
technical reality. (In my entire career, I only ever met ONE Senior Manager
who really understood IT and was capable of discussing the intimate details
of Technology. When he retired, they outsourced the lot because nobody else
(including the official IT Manager) could deal with it.Last I heard they
were very happy with the service from EDS...

>
> It seems that the goal of the designers of COBOL has been tossed out.
> Their goal was to design a language that the average clerk in a company
> could use.

That may well have been ONE of the goals. There was much more interest in
finding a way to develop programs that were not locked in to each individual
platform (as Assembler certainly was) and COBOL was initially sold on its
"platform independence" and "ease of maintenance", rather than as a
scripting language for company administrators.

(Actually, if somebody was to re-invent it as a "scripting language for
company administrators" I think it would probably do pretty well...<G>)

>In this it appears that they have achieved their goals
> admirably. Why do modern language designers not design a language that
> is obvious, easy, powerfull and can be used by anyone without the need
> to tack half the letters of the alphabet behind their name?

Because then there would be no exorbitant fees for consultants and inflated
salaries for programmers...<G>.

If it was easy, and anybody could do it, they wouldn't need us, would they
<G>?

Sadly, it IS getting easier, and NEARLY anybody can do it (see people
expecting to have spreadsheets and databases on their desktops) and that is
why the people in this forum are a dying breed. (The refusal to make effort
and embrace change doesn't help...<G>)

User interfaces and software can only get easier and more intuitive.
Hardware can only get more powerful. In other words, computers will get
"smarter", and the need for in-depth Technical knowledge will diminish as
the "Knowledge Base" takes over from the Engineer. Extrapolate these trends,
and the answer is inevitable: "Computer Programming" was a phenomenon of the
latter half of the 20th Century. [...said it before; I say it again <G>].
By 2020 it will be gone.

(While the number of COBOL programmers has been declining each year, it is
interesting to note that the number of Programming jobs in general is NOT
expanding as rapidly as we might have anticipated.  Today there are 935
programming jobs on the UK Jobserve server. 98 of these are for COBOL.
(11.875%).  In 1999 at this time of year there were 18,000 and  around 35%
involved COBOL (probably inflated by the need for Y2K people.) The point is
that programming in general is becoming less necessary for the average
commercial concern. Outsourcing and packages are becoming much more viable
alternatives.

>
> > Is it really NEW or is it "libraries" and such repackaged?  No - it is
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> will get it at once without the need for years of study.

The Unification of Physics and GUTs and TOEs in general are not expected
anytime soon.  It is expected to be able to represent it in a few equations,
but no-one is expecting them to be simple... Despite the fact that the best
minds on the Planet are working on it, the tools for empirical research are
not available and  are unlikely to be for several hundred years yet,  if
ever...(a cyclotron big enough to get to Grand Unification energies would
require more power than is available in the entire solar system...). Without
such devices it is impossible to study ALL the leptons, hadrons and bosons
which keep popping in and out of what we call reality. So that leaves us
with Theories that cannot be tested... (Bit like debugging by going Live,
isn't it?<G>).

So, summing up, with the axiomatic decline of  commercial computer
programming there is an argument for not even bothering to learn OO.

Whether anyone decides to do so or not will depend on where they expect
their career to go. I have endeavoured to persuade you that the Procedural
boat has some serious holes in it and the pumps are failing. I could be
wrong; but I might not be....  As God said to Noah when he asked for a clue
as to why he was being required to build the Ark: "How long can you tread
water?" (Well,... that's Bill Cosby's version <G>).

It is really silly to argue about OO here. (that's why I've stopped...). No
minds are likely to be changed.

Maybe OO and Java are an inflatable liferaft that will simply delay the
inevitable, but then again, the more time you have afloat, the more chance
there is of rescue...

Pete.
```

```
Then the first question is - "Why is it that OO is not managed properly so
often?".   I suspect the primary reason is that many people are programming Java
(or C++ or whatever OO language) as opposed to programming OO.   I suspect a
secondary reason is that it is seen as a cure for all ills and that all
characteristics of OO need to be implemented to make it work.

At any rate it IS fair to judge a methodology (or doxology or whatever) by
actual results.   These results should not be measured in select samples that
"get it", but should be measured in the whole marketplace.    This is comparable
to someone claiming that his product is safe - if used properly - when in fact
users don't use it properly and have accidents.   The results are what matters.

Once the first question is answered - then pundits will be able to determine the
best way to get OO's benefits used more widely.

> suggested.)

tell people to change?   Is the solution to assume that only some people will be
able to be successful?   Programming by the elite?

Or will the solution be to continue automating the process so that the
granularity of our programming elements continues to get larger and larger?  
(probably)


> Languages are made "de rigeur" by Management, who, in turn, for the  most
> part, are heavily influenced by what they read in the computer press, or
```

```
> 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> records as it is already in sorted sequence when I split it.

Is there a reason you didn't use SUM FIELDS=NONE instead of ICETOOL to
get rid of the dupes? The reason I ask is that using S F=N will result
in the correct record count being printed in DFSORT's SYSPRINT. You
could then define SYSPRINT as a disk dataset and read it in a later
step to create the cntl cards for the util you would use to split the
file.
> 
> Is there a way to get a dataset attributes specifically the size with COBOL
> LE on Z/OS. If I can get the file size and divide it by the record length
> wich is fixed block I can calculate exactly how many records it contain and
> create sysin cards for idcams to split the file into 2.

I think listcat gives that info. Don't forget to factor into the calc
the unused space on each track (depends on the blksize you're using),
including IRGs.
> 
> I need to find out how many records the file contains without reading
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> Henk
```

#### ↳ Re: File size / record count

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-01T14:44:49-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7badnUZLxfal-IDdRVn-sA@giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<401bd5b0.0@news1.mweb.co.za>`

```
Henk wrote:
> Hi
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> records as it is already in sorted sequence when I split it.

IF the reason for splitting the file is media capacity, DONT split the file.
Write output until the output media fills, then switch to new media. This
technique has two advantages:

1. For some reason records may be deleted in the future shrinking the output
to fit on only one tape (disk, diskette, etc.).

2. You'll be set when the file expands to fill THREE output devices.
```

#### ↳ Re: File size / record count

- **From:** Frank Yaeger <yaeger@us.ibm.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-02T09:34:04-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<401E8A0C.6090000@us.ibm.com>`
- **References:** `<401bd5b0.0@news1.mweb.co.za>`

```
Henk wrote:
> Hi
> 
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
> Henk

Take a look at the DFSORT/ICETOOL job in the last post of this thread:

http://www.mainframeforum.com/t625752.html

It shows how to split an input file as evenly as possible into four 
output files with contiguous records (e.g. 1-100, 101-200, etc)using the 
SPLITBY=n parameter of OUTFIL.  You could do the same kind of thing for 
two parts.  It does requires a COPY pass to get the count of the 
records, but DFSORT copy is very fast.

By the way, if you can determine the total number of records without 
reading them, you could just as easily set up a DFSORT job to split the 
files (using SPLITBY=n or STARTREC/ENDREC) as an IDCAMS job.

Frank Yaeger - DFSORT Team  (IBM) - yaeger@us.ibm.com
Specialties: ICETOOL, OUTFIL, Symbols, Migration
=> DFSORT/MVS is on the Web at http://www.ibm.com/storage/dfsort
```

#### ↳ Re: File size / record count

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@sunvaley0.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T15:46:23+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<112fac379749e608a9b27ae913685e5d@news.teranews.com>`
- **References:** `<401bd5b0.0@news1.mweb.co.za>`

```
There is a way go obtain the file size on a file that permits random reads
and has no deleted records. Use 'binary search' type logic, starting with
a value greater than the possible last record. Consider successful reads
as a 'low' and invalid key reads as 'high'. When you get to the 'not found'
point of the search, you are at the last record or last record +1, depending
on whether the last read was 'low' or 'high', respectively.

The number of reads should be int(log2(first-read-nbr)) +1.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Rogue coders to highjack the 2004 election?

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T15:47:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bvofr8$77h$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`
- **References:** `<2bko10peaej7iou2kk9vlecds11s9v8ae9@4ax.com> <TY2dnTWpxfyzWYDd4p2dnA@comcast.com> <euur10pjvdfm473f9laggk2m6hl4k1ahbg@4ax.com> <laSdnRzrHcoo04Pd4p2dnA@giganews.com> <fl5t105kkcflv8dj77h8fjkvu75tvkfv1f@4ax.com>`

```

On  2-Feb-2004, Habitant <berlutte@sympatico.ca> wrote:

> >There is no federal election in the U.S. (except by the Electoral College).
> >ALL elections are done under the authority of each state.
>
> How inconvenient!

Maybe so.    It was done so for good reasons, but as a business problem it did
have the following huge advantage that I hadn't thought of before the last
presidential election:

Consider that the popular vote for the country was about as close as the popular
vote for Florida was.    But nobody wanted to recount the votes in most states,
as those states weren't close.   Heck, some states had hundreds of thousands of
absentee ballots uncounted - that couldn't have made a difference even if they
were 100% for one candidate.

If we had had a single national popular vote, they would have been counting
chads all over the country.

This is something to think of when anybody designs a national ballot system.  
There are business advantages to isolating components of the election.    Heck,
this is an issue that is important with lots of business decisions that
programmers and analysts need to account for.
```

## Thread: COBOL FAQ — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Meta: FAQs, group policy, charter`](topics.md#meta)_

### COBOL FAQ

- **From:** wmklein@ix.netcom.com (William M. Klein)
- **Date:** 2004-02-02T09:09:14+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol,news.answers,comp.answers
- **Message-ID:** `<computer-lang/cobol-faq_1075712916@rtfm.mit.edu>`

```
Archive-name: computer-lang/cobol-faq
Posting-Frequency: twice a month
Last-Modified: 2002/05/06
Version: 3.03
URL: http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm
Reply-To: wmklein@ix.netcom.com


                            COBOL FAQ
                  (Frequently Asked Questions)

Last-Modified: Spring 2002

The full COBOL FAQ can be viewed at:

  http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm

If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, please send
private email to:

    wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com

Toward the top of the FAQ is a pointer to the appendix listing the most
recent significant updates and changes.

This FAQ answers such questions as (and addresses topics such as):

 - Where can I get a COBOL compiler? 
 - Is there a free COBOL compiler? 
 - Where can I contact... ?
 - What is happening with the draft of the next COBOL Standard and what
is in it? 
 - What about OO COBOL? 
 - Books about COBOL
 - COBOL Tools
 - What can/should I post in the COBOL newsgroups?
 - What about USAGE? COMP? Storage for data in xyz format? etc?
 - How do I get started with COBOL? Where can I get education?
Tutorials? Etc

and much, MUCH more
```

## Thread: Reqd help in HP-Cobol — 2 msgs

### Reqd help in HP-Cobol

- **From:** saurabh_khera@dell.com (saurabh)
- **Date:** 2004-02-02T03:12:58-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<74c496a0.0402020312.645563c@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi,

I want some help in cobol.
I am Calling a Subprogram within a Program to validate the Date.
For this I am writing
Call "subProg" of Main Prog using some date-field of some ipm structure.

After compiling I get the error as Odd Address Byte Parameter.
Also Date-field and the fields in that SubProgram are of same size.
Can you tell me why this comes and how it get solve.

Thanx,

Saurabh Khera
```

#### ↳ Re: Reqd help in HP-Cobol

- **From:** Bernard Giroud <bgiroud@free.fr>
- **Date:** 2004-02-02T21:34:02+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<401EB43A.902E7EDF@free.fr>`
- **References:** `<74c496a0.0402020312.645563c@posting.google.com>`

```
saurabh a ï¿½crit :

> Hi,
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Check the alignment of the passed field (should probably
be aligned on a 2, 4 or 8 bytes boundary). If it is not, and you
can't align it, move to a temporary declared at level 01 or 77.

>
> Thanx,
>
> Saurabh Khera
```

#### ↳ Re: End of Line?.....

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2004-02-02T19:07:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0402021907.3fcebb60@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<bvml8i$2ceb$1@justice.itsc.cuhk.edu.hk>`

```
"ï¿½Qï¿½ï¿½" <fifteen@cuhk.edu.hk> wrot

> Excuse me, I am new to COBOL and I want to ask a silly question. Are there
> any End of Line or String in COBOL?.... Since I want the line be terminated
> earlier...(No trailing spaces)

Where is it that you want the 'line of string' terminated earlier ?

The source code ?  A display ?  an output file ?

If it is an output file then you probably want the file with
ORGANIZATION LINE SEQUENTIAL.  However this may, or may not, give
trailing spaces depending on the version of the compiler.

As you have made no mention of the system you are using, the compiler
vendor, the version, or what it is you actually want then it is
difficult to make any useful suggestions.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: End of Line?.....

```
The Micro Focus Net Express file handler has a configuration option
'STRIPSPACE' that controls whether trailing spaces are written or
truncated on line sequential and line advancing files.
```

## Thread: Problemen met indexed bestand en lezen ervan. — 1 msgs

### Problemen met indexed bestand en lezen ervan.

- **From:** peeters.charly@skynet.be (Charly)
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T08:33:45-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1495a4e4.0402030833.7e68d391@posting.google.com>`

```
Ik ben een programma aan het schrijven die een vragen spel is, de
eerste vraag heeft een index 0001 ik geef deze in, de vraag wordt
gesteld bij een goed antw zal de tweede vraag moeten gestled worden,
maar ik zie dat zelf als ik manueel de nieuwe index dus 0002 ingeef
nog steeds vraag 0001 wordt gesteld.

Ik heb de fout al gezocht maar vind deze niet, een automatisch systeem
dat ik hed ingesteld verhoogde een teller met een en zette dit met
move in de index. Dit werkte maar hetzelfde probleem met dat manueel
invoeren.

Ik post hier dan bij mijn code, mischien vindt er een van julie de weg
om zo naar vraag twee te gaan enz.

ps: Kennen julie geen versie van cobol dat op windows draait? Fujitsu
cobol doet vervend en ik werk daar niet graag mee. Nu gebruik ik CB
een compiler maar ik em daar geen info van alleen dat dat snel vast
looopt.

Bedankt, Charly

000005 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
000010  PROGRAM-ID. VRAAG-SPEL.
000011
000012  AUTHOR. Charly, Peeters.
000013  DATE-WRITTEN. 02-02-2004.
000015 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
000016* CONFIGURATION SECTION.
000019  INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
000020  FILE-CONTROL.
000021   SELECT VRAGEN-BEST ASSIGN TO "A:VRAGEN.DAT"
000022    ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED
000023     ACCESS MODE IS DYNAMIC
000024      RECORD KEY IS VRAAG-ID.
000025 DATA DIVISION.
000026  FILE SECTION.
000027  FD VRAGEN-BEST.
000028	01 VRAAG-RECORD.
000029   02 VRAAG-ID        picture XXXX.
000030   02 VRAAG PIC X(70).
000031      
000032   02 ANTWOORD.
000033      03 A PIC X(20).
000034      03 B PIC X(20).
000035      03 C PIC X(20).
000036      03 D PIC X(20).
000037   02 JUIST-ANTW PIC A.
000038             
000100  WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
000101    01 TELLER PIC 9999 VALUE 0001.
000102    01 KEUZE PIC A.
000103    01 BUFFER PIC 9 VALUE 0. 
000200		01 DUMMY PIC X.
000201
000300* LINKAGE SECTION.
000400 PROCEDURE  DIVISION.
000500* DECLARATIVES.
000600* END DECLARATIVES.
000601
000700  MAIN.
000701        
000702  OPEN INPUT VRAGEN-BEST.
000703  DISPLAY "Hier komen de vragen aan."
000704   MOVE TELLER TO VRAAG-ID.  
000705   PERFORM READ-VRAGEN UNTIL BUFFER=1.
        
000708  CLOSE VRAGEN-BEST.
000709  
        READ-VRAGEN.
          
          DISPLAY VRAAG-ID "geef deze in:".
          ACCEPT VRAAG-ID.
         READ VRAGEN-BEST
          INVALID KEY DISPLAY "ERROR"
000706    NOT INVALID KEY PERFORM VRAGEN-PERFORM
000707   END-READ.
        ADD 1 TO BUFFER.

        END-READ-VRAGEN.
000710
000711 
000712
000817
000900 VRAGEN-PERFORM.

000000  DISPLAY "Vraag"VRAAG-ID.
000901  DISPLAY SPACE.
        DISPLAY VRAAG.
000902  DISPLAY "A. " A "B. " B "C. " C "D. " D.
000903  DISPLAY "Keuze:".
000904  ACCEPT KEUZE.
000905  IF KEUZE = JUIST-ANTW 
000906   THEN DISPLAY "Juist" 
000000         ADD 1 TO TELLER
000000          
000907   ELSE DISPLAY "Fout"
000908  END-IF.

000909 END-VRAGEN-PERFORM.
 
000909* VRAAG-LUS.
000   *  IF BUFFER >= 1
      *  THEN PERFORM VRAGEN-PERFORM
      *  END-IF.
000910  EINDE.
001000   DISPLAY "Druk op een toest om af te sluiten."
001001      	ACCEPT DUMMY.
001002     STOP RUN.
001003
```

## Thread: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events — 21 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T17:52:27+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com>`

```
Hi all,


I have the following problem related with Fujitsu COBOL and events
raised by COM objects.

Basically I have a small app that is calling a third party app, and
this app as most Windows apps has the following
1- Methods
2- Properties
3- Events.

I am able to deal with 1 and 2 fine, but I canï¿½t find a way of dealing
with 3.

Example of what is required.

 ENVIRONMENT     DIVISION.
 DATA            DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01 WK                    PIC X(80).
 01 CApplication  OBJECT REFERENCE COM.
 PROCEDURE       DIVISION.
     Move "appname.Application.9" TO WK.
     INVOKE COM "CREATE-OBJECT" USING WK RETURNING CApplication.
     INVOKE cApplication "PrintRecords".

On this particular case the application will fire an event
"record_printed", and if this was VB I could code

private sub appname_record_printed()
   some vbcode e.g. for a progress indicator
end sub


But I am unable to translate this to "*COM".

Is there anyone that can help on this subject, as Fujitsu Support will
charge just to look at this, and will not guarantee a result, as this
is considered a "how-to" which is not covered under the maintenance
contract.




Frederico Fonseca
ema il: frederico_fonseca at syssoft-int.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events

- **From:** thaneh@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell)
- **Date:** 2004-02-03T23:58:05-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bfdfc3e8.0402032358.1548fafd@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com>`

```
Frederico,

Lee Unteriener and I went over this numerous times.  There's just no
way (because of the recursion restriction) to make this work directly.
 The COM server sinks for events just are not supported - outside of
POWER COBOL.  PowerCOBOL CAN handle them as far as I am aware.

NOTE: In and out of process servers behave differently in this respect
too.

May I ask which COM server you are using and is it an in or out of
process server?

I have worked in my capacity at Flexus in helping to ensure these
things DO work with Flexus Sp2 products.  The Sp2 ActiveX support has
been recently updated to support COM, both in and out of process
servers.  We have event handling for in process servers - even those
that are non insertable.  Out of process servers ... someday.

If you happen to be an sp2 user and want more information on this
support - or want to become an sp2 user, please - visit
http://www.flexus.com.

Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com> wrote in message news:<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com>...

> 
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> ema il: frederico_fonseca at syssoft-int.com
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events

- **From:** "Peter E.C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>

```
Drop the component directly on your PowerCOBOL form.

The event you are trying to detect will be displayed in the list of events.
It is simple and easy.

You can also use the Methods and Properties directly, by the same mechanism.

PowerCOBOL is extreme good stuff. You can sometimes place components onto an
invisible PowerCOBOL form and then CALL the form from NETCOBOL... This works
pretty well.

I'm not sure that it is "impossible" to trap events with NetCOBOL (although
I have immense respect for both Thane and Lee); I seem to remember some time
ago trapping a custom event outside PowerCOBOL, but I don't have time at the
moment to re-investigate it. (Events often behave just like properties...)

When I get more time (yeah, right...<G>) I 'll try and find the stuff I did
on this.

Cheers,

Pete.
```

```
Your users can now design or edit reports at runtime with the
```

```
move obj-b to sp2-oc-object-ptr
move 3 to sp2-oc-options
call "SP2" using sp2-set-ocx sp2-ocx-parm
etc etc..
there's some other fill in stuff based on what the type is and such,
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events

- **From:** thaneh@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell)
- **Date:** 2004-02-04T15:53:00-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bfdfc3e8.0402041553.29095d81@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com> <bfdfc3e8.0402032358.1548fafd@posting.google.com> <t4d12058sksonu5ml7jj4s7qmn023cnlqd@4ax.com>`

```
I've not used that particular product.  

Does it show as something that can be inserted into the PowerCOBOL
form?  If not - I think you are going to be really out of luck!  I
know v8 was still an ActiveX control (still COM) - what matters is if
v9 is "insertable" or not.

If it is, then in order to process events I think you will need to use
PowerCOBOL directly as it proxies them.

As I said - we never (and Lee and I worked hard at it) were able to
make Event sinks work with "regular" Fujitsu COBOL.  There may still
be a way.

Here's what I know.  With COM you can setup COM SERVERS that act as
LISTENERs for other COM server events.  A routine is invoked in your
new COM server by the event firing on the "existing" one.  You have to
make an API call to "register" for the notifications of the events and
provide the name of the invoked routine.

With this work with Fujitsu generated COM servers?  I dunno.  Even if
it does - can you handle the communication between the two processes
back to your main form?  I dunno.

Have you considered a switch to Sp2 at any point in the future.  This
really is not a shameless plug.  It's just that sp2 allows the GUI,
the COM/ActiveX interface and all that and is completely compiler
independant.  You can then change compilers at will and won't be
locked into a particular compiler vendor.

For those that argue that now you are locked into Flexus and sp2 - if
there is concern over the future, Flexus offers a third party source
code escrow - for a fee.  If you participate and something happenes to
Flexus - you get the source.


Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com> wrote in message news:<t4d12058sksonu5ml7jj4s7qmn023cnlqd@4ax.com>...
> Hi Thane,
> 
…[83 more quoted lines elided]…
> ema il: frederico_fonseca at syssoft-int.com
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-05T12:02:45+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e394205dc0jp94t9dmko17qp1r9v6h372u@4ax.com>`

```
Paulo, Frederico,

I am amazed that you have both had such problems with PowerCOBOL.

I've used it for years (since version 3) and it has always done what it is
supposed to.

The solution of writing a VBX control and dropping it into PowerCOBOL, while
a very good idea, should be unnecessary.

I write ActiveX/COM controls in PowerCOBOL all the time and find it
excellent for this.

It DOES take a little getting used to, but anyone with a VB background
should have no problem adapting to it, as the environments are very similar.

I have found the documentation you complain of, to be adequate for
developing and using the product, but not so, inasmuch as it sometimes
produces message boxes which are undocumented and there are no clues as to
what is wrong.. (As both of you write excellent English, I guess it isn't a
language problem?)

I agree completely about the lack of adequate support from Fujitsu and this
is probably why you have developed an aversion to it. I found that on the
one occasion when I really needed their help, there was no-one there who
could provide an answer to the problems we had, and it meant re-writing a
large amount of code in OO COBOL (NetCOBOL). Much of it could be cut and
pasted from PowerCOBOL but it was still an experience I don't ever want to
have to do again.

It is likely that Fujitsu will drop it in the next year or two and, I for
one, will be sorry to see it go.

Pete.
```

```
==================== quote ====================

"Thane Hubbell" <thaneh@softwaresimple.com> wrote in message
news:bfdfc3e8.0402052359.2f397dfc@posting.google.com...

Yes, apparently so. Version 8, which I have, could certainly be used with
PowerCOBOL.

However, it does give a warning when dropping the Report Viewer Control into
PowerCOBOL that this component is provided purely for backward compatibility
and may not cope with new features in Crystal Reports. Their preferred
solution is to use the TDC, and they give a reference to their site for
details. Once the warning disappears, the component functions properly and
all its events come up, as you would expect.

Sorry, I'm not up to date with Crystal...

Pete.
==================== end quote ====================

As for Tapi.Tapi, I can use it from PowerCOBOL with no problem. A COM server
doesn't HAVE to be dropped on a PowerCOBOL form to be usable from one. In
fact, I have a number of PowerCOBOL applications that call inprocess servers
without problem.

(I have never been able to get out-of-process servers working from
PowerCOBOL, even when using DLLHost.exe as a surrogate process, although
this works fine from NetCOBOL (Context configuring has to be provided for
the out of process servers)).

Having said that, I have moved away from Tapi.Tapi as it is too low a level
and provides many features and interfaces that I don't want or need. (Like
media etc.). I am currently using a much simpler .OCX called VoiceAngel,
that provides exactly the Methods, Properties, and Events, required for IVR
and Telephony in general.  As soon as the Helpfile in English is finished
(I am currently working on it), I will recommend this component here. It
will also have sample code and examples in COBOL (as well as VB, Java, and
C++), which few components do.

Pete.
```

```
I've done similar work with C++ - the MFC activex control wrapper
makes it fairly easy to import COM type libraries and generate the
proxies.  However, there is a big problem sometimes.  Some controls
will throw events that expect a response - you need to get into some
tricky thread work to make the proxy go back to your developed control
- talk to your form - get a response then return the event responses
appropriately.

For MOST COM servers this isn't an issue - they don't have this
interactive type of event - but some do, and it's often not clear
which they are.


Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com> wrote in message news:<kck620h101sevbb4rfo4biursvnf42rasc@4ax.com>...
> On 5 Feb 2004 05:31:41 -0800, pvieira@emporsoft.pt (Paulo Vieira)
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events - Found the solution

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-14T20:39:07+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<s61t20l58i08t09id4f0s85q41hvbmdber@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com>`

```


Solution to the problem at the bottom.

On Tue, 03 Feb 2004 17:52:27 +0000, Frederico Fonseca
<real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com> wrote:

>Hi all,
>
…[33 more quoted lines elided]…
>But I am unable to translate this to "*COM".


First thanks to all the helped on this subject.

Based on what Thane said , and on an example supplied by Paulo, I
managed to solve this problem by following the following steps.

1- Create a small VB OCX that can be inserted and has events that can
be processed by POWER COBOL. Source at the very end.
This control returns an event for each event raised by the Crystal
Report being processed.

2- add this OCX to the POWER form and assign the Crystal Report object
to one of it's properties.

3- Add all the code that needs to be on a CR event to the OCX events.


Regards

Frederico Fonseca



VBCODE

VERSION 5.00
Begin VB.UserControl evWrapper 
   BackColor       =   &H80000005&
   ClientHeight    =   1176
   ClientLeft      =   0
   ClientTop       =   0
   ClientWidth     =   1776
   ScaleHeight     =   1176
   ScaleWidth      =   1776
End
Attribute VB_Name = "evWrapper"
Attribute VB_GlobalNameSpace = False
Attribute VB_Creatable = True
Attribute VB_PredeclaredId = False
Attribute VB_Exposed = True
Dim oreport As CRAXDRT.Report
Dim WithEvents oSection1 As CRAXDRT.Section
Attribute oSection1.VB_VarHelpID = -1
Dim WithEvents oSection2 As CRAXDRT.Section

Public Event CREventSectionFormat()
Private activesection As String
Public Property Let cr_report_object(cr_report As CRAXDRT.Report)
Dim index As Integer
Set oreport = cr_report
index = oreport.Sections.Count
If index > 0 Then
   Set oSection1 = oreport.Sections.Item(1)
End If
If index > 1 Then
   Set oSection2 = oreport.Sections.Item(2)
End If
'(More sections can be added)

End Property

Public Property Get cr_report_object() As CRAXDRT.Report
cr_report_object = oreport
End Property
Public Property Let cr_report_active_section(cr_report_section As
String)
cr_report_section = cr_report_section
End Property
Public Property Get cr_report_active_section() As String
cr_report_active_section = activesection
End Property
Private Sub oSection1_Format(ByVal pFormattingInfo As Object)
    activesection = oSection1.Name
    cr_report_activesection = activesection
    RaiseEvent CREventSectionFormat
End Sub
Private Sub oSection2_Format(ByVal pFormattingInfo As Object)
    activesection = oSection2.Name
    cr_report_activesection = activesection
    RaiseEvent CREventSectionFormat
End Sub
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL and COM and events - Found the solution

- **From:** "Peter E.C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2004-02-15T10:54:44+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<402e99ef_7@news.athenanews.com>`
- **References:** `<manv105c1q959lkbdqn5dknsm145ditq5n@4ax.com> <s61t20l58i08t09id4f0s85q41hvbmdber@4ax.com>`

```

wrote the "OCX" in powerCOBOL instead of VB.

Pete.
```

### Microfocus ignoring initcall when using cobsql?

- **From:** psacha@web.de (Philipp Sacha)
- **Date:** 2004-02-04T05:37:10-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<53a9c2bd.0402040537.44fc2436@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi,

i am trying to access an oracle 9i database from mf cobol. I have
created the shared library and tried to use with initcall"rdbmslib"
but the initcall statement seemed to be ignored:

cob -v -C 'INITCALL"rdbmslib" preprocess(cobsql) CSQLT=ORACLE' -o
sqltest1.o -k sqltest1.cbl
cob32 -C nolist -v -C INITCALL"rdbmslib" preprocess(cobsql)
CSQLT=ORACLE -o sqltest1.o -k sqltest1.cbl

* Micro Focus COBSQL Integrated Preprocessor with ASCII/EBCDIC Support

* CSQL-I-018: Invoking ORACLE8 Precompiler/Translator

* CSQL-I-001: Cobsql has finished returning to the Checker
* Total Messages:     0
* Data:        1104     Code:         752


When i do a nm to the resulting sqltest1.o i see that a lot of symbols

nm sqltest1.o
         U SQLADR
         U SQLBEX
00000000 T SQLTEST1
         U _mFgAE
         U _mFgF805
         U _mFgF806
         U _mFginitdat
         U _mFgprogchain
         U _mFgprogcheckexit
         U _mFgprogunchain

         U _mFldhandle

00000000 T sqltest1


Even when giving an inexistent file to initcall like initcall"foo" the

Any hints?

Regards
Philipp Sacha
```

#### ↳ Re: Microfocus ignoring initcall when using cobsql?

- **From:** "Simon Tobias" <Simon.Tobias@nospam.microfocus.com>
- **Date:** 2004-02-04T14:10:26
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bvr0u8$mbg$1@hyperion.microfocus.com>`
- **References:** `<53a9c2bd.0402040537.44fc2436@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi Philipp.

From a quick glance at the command-line you've used :

cob -v -C 'INITCALL"rdbmslib" preprocess(cobsql) CSQLT=ORACLE' -o
sqltest1.o -k sqltest1.cbl

You are, by default, creating an int code module. If you really intend to
create an object file, you must pass -xc to the cob command line.

The INITCALL directive will effectively force a load of "rdbmslib" at
execution-time, rather than at compile-time, so a non-existant file will
only be detected when you execute your application.

In addition, to pass CSQLT=ORACLE from the cob command line, you must
specify == rather than =, as the shell may misinterpret the equals sign.

Hope this helps.

SimonT.
```

#### ↳ Re: A Kind of XML parser ??? (like Java)

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2004-02-05T14:32:43+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fusUb.404$PY.151@newssvr26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<4096148f.0402050105.28c56df4@posting.google.com>`

```
"JR" <jorenders@hotmail.com> wrote in message
news:4096148f.0402050105.28c56df4@posting.google.com...
> Does anybody know of you can read a xml
> file intelligently with a Cobol program.
> How can you tell cobol that a tag 25 times
> returns and etc...

If your O/S is windows or Unix, the expat parser (freeware) can be used, as
long as you can supply a callback address (PROCEDURE-POINTER) with your
particular COBOL compiler. You'll also need to handle your own data storage
, which will require either dynamic memory allocation/de-allocation OR you
can write the data to a disk file  (counting tags as you go, if you'd like)
and get your tag values back from that file later.

No, it is not real simple if you haven't done this kind of programming
before, but expat is fast, reliable and the price is certainly right.

MCM
```

```
Here's one that I got from the net and modified. It is called as a
subroutine with the XML passed to it.  For any serious work you may
need to change this.

      *--Version: 4.10  30/07/02  10:46:58

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID.             xmlparse.

      *    xmlparse.LST
      *    \xml\xml.cbl

      *AUTHOR. Miami-Dade Community College.
      *DATE-WRITTEN.  July, 2000.
      *DATE-COMPILED.
      *REMARKS.
      *
      *    LAST CHANGE:  09/12/00 12:02:24 SAHWC
      *
      *    This program will parse any valid XML document into its
      *    component parts.
      *

       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
       FILE-CONTROL.

       DATA DIVISION.
       FILE SECTION.

       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.

       01  FILLER.
           05  FILLER                  PIC X(32) VALUE
               'WORKING-STORAGE FOR XMLPARSE>>>:'.
           05  WK-INDEX                PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  WK-INDEX-1              PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  WK-INDEX-2              PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  WK-START-INDEX          PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  WK-SEQ-NBR              PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  ENDING-PTR              PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  BASE-PTR                PIC S9(9)           COMP SYNC.
           05  WK-LENGTH               PIC S9(4)           COMP SYNC.
           05  ENTITY-LENGTH           PIC S9(4)           COMP SYNC.
           05  RESULT                  PIC 9.
           05  WK-FIND-CHAR            PIC X.
           05  SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-CHECK  PIC X.
           05  WK-ENTITY               PIC X(6).
           05  FILLER REDEFINES WK-ENTITY.
               10  WK-ENTITY-X         PIC X     OCCURS 6 TIMES.
           05  WK-MARKUP-CHARACTER     PIC X.
           05  ATTR-NAME               PIC X(50).
           05  ELEM-NAME               PIC X(50).
           05  DATA-VALUE              PIC X(1010).
           05  FILLER REDEFINES DATA-VALUE.
               10  DATA-VALUE-X        PIC X     OCCURS 1010 TIMES.
           05  NAME-VALUE              PIC X(1000).
           05  FILLER REDEFINES NAME-VALUE.
               10  NAME-VALUE-X        PIC X     OCCURS 1000 TIMES.

           05  WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH PIC X.
               88  WK-PARSING-ERROR              VALUE '1'.

       01  ToUpper.
           03  Char-Comp               PIC 9(4) COMP SYNC.

               05  FILLER              PIC X.
               05  Char-X              PIC X.

      *        10  FILLER              PIC X.
      *        10  LEFT-BRACKET        PIC X.
      *    05  RITE-BRACKET-X          PIC S9(4) VALUE 189 COMP SYNC.
      *    05  FILLER REDEFINES RITE-BRACKET-X.
      *        10  FILLER              PIC X.
      *        10  RITE-BRACKET        PIC X.
      *    05  VALUE-TAB-X             PIC S9(4) VALUE 5   COMP SYNC.
      *    05  FILLER REDEFINES VALUE-TAB-X.
      *        10  FILLER              PIC X.
      *        10  VALUE-TAB           PIC X.
      *    05  VALUE-LF-X              PIC S9(4) VALUE 37 COMP SYNC.
      *    05  FILLER REDEFINES VALUE-LF-X.
      *        10  FILLER              PIC X.
      *        10  VALUE-LF            PIC X.
      *    05  VALUE-CR-X              PIC S9(4) VALUE 13 COMP SYNC.
      *    05  FILLER REDEFINES VALUE-CR-X.
      *        10  FILLER              PIC X.
      *        10  VALUE-CR            PIC X.

      *    ASCII values
           05  LEFT-BRACKET            PIC X     VALUE "<".
           05  RITE-BRACKET            PIC X     VALUE ">".
           05  VALUE-TAB               PIC X     VALUE x"09".
           05  VALUE-LF                PIC X     VALUE x"0A".

           05  RESULT-TABLE.
               10  FILLER              PIC X(3)  VALUE '1  '.

               10  FILLER              PIC X(3)  VALUE '111'.
               10  FILLER              PIC X(3)  VALUE '111'.
           05  FILLER REDEFINES RESULT-TABLE.
               10  FILLER                        OCCURS 9 TIMES.
                   15  FILLER          PIC X.
                       88  ELEM-NAME-REQUIRED    VALUE '1'.
                   15  FILLER          PIC X.
                       88  ATTR-NAME-REQUIRED    VALUE '1'.
                   15  FILLER          PIC X.
                       88  DATA-VALUE-REQUIRED   VALUE '1'.

       LINKAGE SECTION.

           COPY "xmlparse.ws".     *> \az\include\xmlparse.ws

       PROCEDURE DIVISION USING XML-Interface
                                XML-Document
                                .
       Program-XMLParse.

           MOVE '0'            TO WK-END-OF-MSG-SWITCH
                                  WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH

           IF ( XML-RESERVED = ZEROES )
               MOVE ZERO       TO CHAR-PTR
                                  WK-SEQ-NBR
               MOVE 00         TO STATE
               MOVE 6          TO RESULT
           END-IF

           PERFORM MAIN-RTN
               UNTIL WK-END-OF-MSG
                  OR WK-PARSING-ERROR

           IF ( WK-PARSING-ERROR )
               PERFORM PARSED-DATA-RTN
               PERFORM PARSING-ERROR-RTN
           END-IF

           MOVE ZERO           TO RETURN-CODE
           .

           EXIT PROGRAM
           .

       MAIN-RTN.

           ADD 1                   TO CHAR-PTR

           IF ( STATE > 00 AND < 07 )
               PERFORM PARSED-DATA-RTN
           END-IF
           .

           IF ( CHAR-PTR > XML-LENGTH
      *      OR          > 9216
              )
               MOVE '1'             TO WK-END-OF-MSG-SWITCH
               PERFORM PARSED-DATA-RTN
           ELSE

               EVALUATE State
               WHEN ZERO
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '<' )
                       MOVE 07         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE 33         TO STATE
                       SUBTRACT 1    FROM CHAR-PTR
                   END-IF

               WHEN 1
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '/' )
                       MOVE 21         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '>' )
                       MOVE 00         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       PERFORM FIND-VALID-FIRST-NAME-RTN
                       IF ( WK-FOUND )
                           MOVE CHAR-PTR   TO BASE-PTR
                           MOVE 27         TO STATE
                       ELSE
                           MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                       END-IF
                   END-IF
                   END-IF

               WHEN 2
               WHEN 3
               WHEN 4
               WHEN 5
               WHEN 6
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 7
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '/' )
                       MOVE 25         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '?' )
                       MOVE 22         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '!' )
                       MOVE 08         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       PERFORM FIND-VALID-FIRST-NAME-RTN
                       IF ( WK-FOUND )
                           MOVE CHAR-PTR   TO BASE-PTR
                           MOVE 20         TO STATE
                       ELSE
                           MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                       END-IF
                   END-IF
                   END-IF
                   END-IF

               WHEN 8
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '-' )
                       MOVE 09         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = LEFT-BRACKET )
                       MOVE 14         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                   END-IF
                   END-IF

               WHEN 9
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '-' )
                       MOVE 10         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                   END-IF

               WHEN 10
                   MOVE '-'            TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 12         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 11
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 12
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '-' )
                       MOVE 13         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE 10         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 13
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '>' )
                       MOVE 00         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE 10         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 14
                   MOVE CHAR-PTR       TO BASE-PTR
                   PERFORM FIND-VALID-NAME-RTN
                   IF ( NAME-VALUE-START-WITH-CDATA )
                       MOVE 15         TO STATE
                   END-IF
                   SUBTRACT 1        FROM CHAR-PTR

               WHEN 15
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = LEFT-BRACKET )
                       MOVE 16         TO STATE
                   END-IF
                   COMPUTE BASE-PTR = CHAR-PTR + 1

               WHEN 16
                   MOVE RITE-BRACKET   TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 18         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 17
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 18
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = RITE-BRACKET )
                       MOVE 19         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE 16         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 19
                   MOVE '>'            TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 02         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE 16         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 20
                   PERFORM FIND-VALID-NAME-RTN
                   MOVE NAME-VALUE     TO ELEM-NAME
                   MOVE 01             TO STATE
                   SUBTRACT 1        FROM CHAR-PTR

               WHEN 21
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '>' )
                       MOVE 03         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 22
                   MOVE '?'            TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 24         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 23
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 24
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '>' )
                       MOVE 00         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 25
                   PERFORM FIND-VALID-FIRST-NAME-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE CHAR-PTR   TO BASE-PTR
                       MOVE 26         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                   END-IF

               WHEN 26
                   PERFORM FIND-VALID-NAME-RTN
                   MOVE NAME-VALUE     TO ELEM-NAME
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '>' )
                       MOVE 05         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 27
                   PERFORM FIND-VALID-NAME-RTN
                   MOVE NAME-VALUE     TO ATTR-NAME
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '=' )
                       MOVE 28         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 28
                   PERFORM SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = VALUE-QUOTE )
                       MOVE 29         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                   IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = '"' )
                       MOVE 31         TO STATE
                   ELSE
                       MOVE '1'        TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH
                   END-IF
                   END-IF
                   COMPUTE BASE-PTR = CHAR-PTR + 1

               WHEN 29
                   MOVE VALUE-QUOTE    TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 04         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 30
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 31
                   MOVE '"'            TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 04         TO STATE
                   END-IF

               WHEN 32
                   CONTINUE

               WHEN 33
                   MOVE CHAR-PTR       TO BASE-PTR
                   MOVE '<'            TO WK-FIND-CHAR
                   PERFORM FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN
                   IF ( WK-FOUND )
                       MOVE 06         TO STATE
                   SUBTRACT 1        FROM CHAR-PTR

               WHEN OTHER
                   MOVE '1'            TO WK-PARSING-ERROR-SWITCH

               END-EVALUATE
           END-IF
           .

       PARSED-DATA-RTN.

           IF ( WK-PARSING-ERROR )
               MOVE 6              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( WK-END-OF-MSG )
               MOVE 5              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 01 )
               MOVE ELEM-NAME      TO SAVE-ELEM-NAME
               MOVE 1              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 02 )
               MOVE SAVE-ELEM-NAME TO ELEM-NAME
               COMPUTE ENDING-PTR = CHAR-PTR - 3
               PERFORM GET-DATA-VALUE-RTN
               MOVE 00             TO STATE
               MOVE 4              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 03 )
               MOVE SAVE-ELEM-NAME TO ELEM-NAME
               MOVE 00             TO STATE
               MOVE 2              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 04 )
               MOVE SAVE-ELEM-NAME TO ELEM-NAME
               COMPUTE ENDING-PTR = CHAR-PTR - 1
               PERFORM GET-DATA-VALUE-RTN
               MOVE ZERO           TO WK-INDEX-1
               PERFORM ENTITY-REFERENCE-RTN
                   VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1 BY 1
                     UNTIL WK-INDEX > 1000
               MOVE 01             TO STATE
               MOVE 3              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 05 )
               MOVE 00             TO STATE
               MOVE 2              TO RESULT
           ELSE
           IF ( STATE = 06 )
               MOVE SAVE-ELEM-NAME TO ELEM-NAME
               MOVE CHAR-PTR       TO ENDING-PTR
               PERFORM GET-DATA-VALUE-RTN
               MOVE ZERO           TO WK-INDEX-1
               PERFORM ENTITY-REFERENCE-RTN
                  VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1 BY 1
                    UNTIL WK-INDEX > 1000

               MOVE 00             TO STATE
               MOVE 4              TO RESULT
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF
           END-IF

           ADD 1                   TO WK-SEQ-NBR

           IF ( WK-SEQ-NBR > SAVE-INDEX )
               MOVE '1'            TO WK-END-OF-MSG-SWITCH
               MOVE WK-SEQ-NBR     TO SAVE-INDEX

               MOVE SPACES         TO XML-PARSED-AREA
               MOVE RESULT         TO XML-RETURN-CODE
               IF ( ELEM-NAME-REQUIRED(RESULT) )
                   MOVE ELEM-NAME  TO XML-ELEMENT-NAME
               END-IF
               IF ( ATTR-NAME-REQUIRED(RESULT) )
                   MOVE ATTR-NAME  TO XML-ATTRIBUTE-NAME
               END-IF
               IF ( DATA-VALUE-REQUIRED(RESULT) )
                   MOVE DATA-VALUE TO XML-DATA-VALUE
               END-IF
           END-IF
           .

       SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-RTN.

           IF ( CHAR-PTR NOT > XML-LENGTH )
               MOVE XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) TO SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-CHECK
               IF ( SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-CHECK = SPACES
                 OR                          VALUE-TAB
                 OR                          VALUE-LF
                 OR                          VALUE-CR
                  )
                   ADD 1           TO CHAR-PTR
               END-IF
           END-IF
           .

       FIND-THIS-CHARACTER-RTN.

           MOVE '0'                TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           PERFORM
               UNTIL CHAR-PTR > XML-LENGTH
                  OR WK-FOUND

               IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR) = WK-FIND-CHAR )
                   MOVE '1'        TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
               ELSE
                   ADD 1           TO CHAR-PTR
               END-IF
           END-PERFORM
           .

       FIND-VALID-FIRST-NAME-RTN.

           MOVE '0'                TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           PERFORM SEARCH-FOR-CHAR-RTN
               VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1 BY 1
                 UNTIL WK-INDEX > TTL-ACCEPTABLE-FIRST-CHARS
                    OR WK-FOUND
            .

       SEARCH-FOR-CHAR-RTN.

           IF ( XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR)
                       = ACCEPTABLE-CHARS-X(WK-INDEX) )
               MOVE '1'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           END-IF
           .

       FIND-VALID-NAME-RTN.

           MOVE '1'                TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           PERFORM
               UNTIL CHAR-PTR > XML-LENGTH
                  OR NOT WK-Found

               MOVE '0'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
               PERFORM SEARCH-FOR-CHAR-RTN
                   VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1 BY 1
                     UNTIL WK-INDEX > TTL-ACCEPTABLE-CHARS
                        OR WK-FOUND
               IF ( WK-FOUND )
                   ADD 1           TO CHAR-PTR
               END-IF
           END-PERFORM

           MOVE ZERO               TO Char-Comp
           MOVE ZERO               TO WK-INDEX-1
           MOVE SPACES             TO NAME-VALUE
           PERFORM MOVE-NAME-VALUE-RTN
               VARYING WK-INDEX FROM BASE-PTR BY 1
                 UNTIL WK-INDEX = CHAR-PTR
           .

       MOVE-NAME-VALUE-RTN.

           ADD 1                   TO WK-INDEX-1
           MOVE XML-DOCUMENT-X(WK-INDEX)
                                   TO Char-X
           IF ( Char-X >= 'a' AND <= 'z' )
               SUBTRACT 32       FROM Char-Comp
           END-IF
           MOVE Char-X             TO NAME-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-1)
           .

       GET-DATA-VALUE-RTN.

           MOVE SPACES             TO DATA-VALUE
           MOVE ZERO               TO WK-INDEX-1
           PERFORM MOVE-DATA-VALUE-RTN
               VARYING WK-INDEX FROM BASE-PTR BY 1
                 UNTIL WK-INDEX = ENDING-PTR

           MOVE '0'                TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           PERFORM REMOVE-DATA-VALUE-RTN
              VARYING WK-INDEX FROM WK-INDEX-1 BY -1
                UNTIL WK-INDEX < 1
                   OR WK-FOUND

           MOVE '0'                TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           MOVE ZERO               TO WK-LENGTH
           PERFORM COUNT-LEADING-SPACES-RTN
               VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1 BY 1
                 UNTIL WK-INDEX > 1000
                    OR DATA-VALUE = SPACES
                    OR WK-FOUND

           IF ( WK-LENGTH > ZERO )
               PERFORM REMOVE-LEADING-SPACES-RTN
                   VARYING WK-INDEX FROM 1  BY 1
                     UNTIL WK-INDEX > 1010
           END-IF
           .

       MOVE-DATA-VALUE-RTN.

           ADD 1                   TO WK-INDEX-1
           MOVE XML-DOCUMENT-X(WK-INDEX) TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-1)
           .

       REMOVE-DATA-VALUE-RTN.

           MOVE DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX) TO SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-CHECK
           IF ( SKIP-WHITE-SPACE-CHECK = SPACES
             OR                          VALUE-TAB
             OR                          VALUE-LF
             OR                          VALUE-CR
              )
               MOVE SPACES         TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX)
           ELSE
               MOVE '1'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           END-IF
           .

       COUNT-LEADING-SPACES-RTN.

           IF ( DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX) = SPACES )
               ADD 1               TO WK-LENGTH
           ELSE
               MOVE '1'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           END-IF
           .

       REMOVE-LEADING-SPACES-RTN.

           ADD 1                   TO WK-LENGTH
           MOVE DATA-VALUE-X(WK-LENGTH)
                                   TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX)
           MOVE SPACES             TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-LENGTH)
           .

       ENTITY-REFERENCE-RTN.

           IF ( DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX) = '&' )
               MOVE '0'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
               MOVE SPACES         TO WK-ENTITY
               MOVE 1              TO ENTITY-LENGTH
               MOVE WK-INDEX       TO WK-INDEX-1
               PERFORM FIND-MARKUP-CHARACTER-RTN
                   6 TIMES

               IF ( WK-FOUND )
                   MOVE '0'        TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
                   MOVE SPACES     TO WK-MARKUP-CHARACTER
                   PERFORM MATCH-ENTITY-RTN
                       VARYING WK-INDEX-1 FROM 1 BY 1
                         UNTIL WK-INDEX-1 > TTL-ENTITY-REFERENCE
                            OR WK-FOUND
               END-IF
               IF ( WK-FOUND )
                   MOVE WK-MARKUP-CHARACTER TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX)
                   COMPUTE WK-START-INDEX = WK-INDEX + 1
                   PERFORM MOVE-DATA-VALUE-UP-RTN
                       VARYING WK-INDEX-1 FROM WK-START-INDEX BY 1
                         UNTIL WK-INDEX-1 > 1100
               END-IF
           END-IF
           .

       FIND-MARKUP-CHARACTER-RTN.

           IF ( WK-INDEX-1 < 1000 )
               IF NOT ( WK-FOUND )
                   MOVE DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-1)
                                   TO WK-ENTITY-X(ENTITY-LENGTH)
               END-IF
               IF ( DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-1) = ';' )
                   MOVE '1'        TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
               ELSE
                   ADD 1           TO WK-INDEX-1
                                      ENTITY-LENGTH
               END-IF
           END-IF
           .

       MATCH-ENTITY-RTN.

           IF ( WK-ENTITY = ENTITY-REFERENCE-X(WK-INDEX-1) )
               MOVE MARKUP-CHARACTER(WK-INDEX-1)
                                   TO WK-MARKUP-CHARACTER
               MOVE '1'            TO WK-FOUND-SWITCH
           END-IF
           .

       MOVE-DATA-VALUE-UP-RTN.

           COMPUTE WK-INDEX-2 = WK-INDEX-1 + ENTITY-LENGTH - 1
           MOVE DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-2)
                                   TO DATA-VALUE-X(WK-INDEX-1)
           .

       PARSING-ERROR-RTN.

           DISPLAY '**************************************************'
           DISPLAY '**************ERROR IN PGM
XMLPARSE***************'
           DISPLAY '**************************************************'
           DISPLAY 'RESULT: '              RESULT
           DISPLAY 'SEQ-NBR: '             WK-SEQ-NBR
           DISPLAY 'STATE: '               STATE
           DISPLAY 'CHAR-PTR: '            CHAR-PTR
           DISPLAY 'BASE-PTR: '            BASE-PTR
           DISPLAY 'ELEM-NAME: '           ELEM-NAME
           DISPLAY 'SAVE-ELEM-NAME: '      SAVE-ELEM-NAME
           DISPLAY 'ATTR-NAME: '           ATTR-NAME
           DISPLAY 'DATA-VALUE: '          DATA-VALUE
           DISPLAY 'NAME-VALUE: '          NAME-VALUE
           DISPLAY 'SAVE-INDEX: '          SAVE-INDEX
           DISPLAY 'XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR): '
                                           XML-DOCUMENT-X(CHAR-PTR)
           DISPLAY 'XML-RETURN-CODE: '     XML-RETURN-CODE
           DISPLAY 'XML-ELEMENT-NAME: '    XML-ELEMENT-NAME
           DISPLAY 'XML-ATTRIBUTE-NAME: '  XML-ATTRIBUTE-NAME
           DISPLAY 'XML-DATA-VALUE: '      XML-DATA-VALUE
           .

      * ================================================================
      *    end of source
      * ================================================================
```

```
  *--Version: 4.10  29/07/02  10:28:09

       01  XML-Interface.
           05  XML-Occurs              PIC 9(9) VALUE 10000.
           05  XML-Length              PIC 9(9).
           05  XML-Reserved.
               10  Save-Index          PIC 9(9).
               10  Char-Ptr            PIC 9(9).
               10  State               PIC 99.
               10  Save-Elem-Name      PIC X(50).
               10  FILLER              PIC X(30).
           05  XML-Parsed-Area.
               10  XML-Return-Code     PIC 9.
```
